Other vertebrates noted: None.--This was a new transect that began at Davis Dam where the river cuts through bedrock and is deep and narrow. It continues south for 2 miles to Laughlin, NV. Throughout this section the river's western bank is composed of 20-30' high bluffs. The east bank is not as steeply or as deeply cut and has a few shoals and gravel bars extending out into the main channel somewhat at times of low water levels such as now. the water is apparently fairly dep here because the entire stretch is frequented by diving ducks - goldeneye, megansers, buffleheads. Redheads, scaup, and Ring-necked Ducks have been seen here previously.	Rare but regular winter visitor from mid-November to early April. Usually occurs with flocks of Common Goldeneyes below Davis and Parker Dams...each winter from 1974 until 1979. Maximum: 57 in December 1974 (p.147).
